10.    Source and Amount of Funds 

The Offer is not conditioned on any financing arrangements or financing contingencies. 

The total amount of funds required by the Purchaser to pay for all outstanding shares of HTE common stock that are tendered in the Offer
and converted into the right to receive cash in the Merger, and to pay all fees and expenses incurred by SunGard and Purchaser related to the Offer and the Merger, is estimated to be approximately $121 million plus any related transaction fees and
expenses. The Purchaser plans to obtain the funds needed for the Offer and the Merger through capital contributions or loans that will be made by SunGard, either directly or through one or more wholly owned subsidiaries of SunGard, to the Purchaser.
To make these contributions or loans, SunGard expects to use its existing cash resources or funds borrowed under its existing line of credit pursuant to its Credit Agreements (described below), or a combination of both. In addition, upon completion
of the Merger, SunGard will have available the cash held by HTE (approximately $
29,595,537 million as of February 
12, 2003) to pay such amounts. 

SunGards line of credit is available pursuant to a 364-Day Credit Agreement, dated as of January 25, 2002 and as amended form time
to time, and an Amended and Restated Three-Year Credit Agreement, dated as of January 10, 2003 (collectively, the Credit Agreements), among SunGard, certain banks and other financial institutions, JPMorgan Chase Bank, as Administrative
Agent, PNC Bank, National Association, as Syndication Agent, First Union National Bank, as Documentation Agent, ABN AMRO Bank, N.V., as Co-Documentation Agent, and Fleet National Bank, as Co-Documentation Agent. The Credit Agreements contain
representations and warranties, conditions precedent, covenants, events of default and other provisions generally found in similar agreements. The Credit Agreements provide for up to $500 million of unsecured borrowings, and consist of a $150
million short-term (364 day) facility that was extended in January 2003 and now expires in January 2004, a $175 million revolving facility and a $175 million term loan that both expire in January 2005. The multi-year agreement was amended in January
2003 to permit $75 million of multicurrency borrowing under the $175 million revolving facility and to add J.P. Morgan Europe Limited, as London Agent, as a party. SunGards only current outstanding borrowings under the Credit Agreements are
$175 million under the term loan. SunGard can periodically designate borrowings as base-rate borrowings or LIBOR borrowings. Base-rate borrowings bear interest generally at the prime rate plus a margin (currently prime), while LIBOR borrowings bear
interest at a rate equal to LIBOR plus a margin (currently LIBOR plus 1%), depending upon SunGards corporate credit rating at the time of the borrowing. Interest rates on base-rate borrowings reset daily, while LIBOR borrowings can be fixed
for one-, two-, three- or six-month periods at SunGards option. In order to remain eligible to 



borrow under the Credit Agreements, SunGard must, among other requirements, maintain a minimum net worth of $850 million plus 50% of the
quarterly net income starting April 1, 2002 ($930 million as of September 30, 2002), an interest coverage ratio of at least four to one, and limit its total debt to no more than two and one-half times SunGards earnings before interest, taxes,
depreciation and amortization. 

The foregoing
summary of the Credit Agreements does not purport to be a complete description of the terms and conditions of the Credit Agreements and is qualified in its entirety by reference to the Credit Agreements, a copy of each of which is filed as an
exhibit to the Tender Offer Statement on Schedule TO that has been filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission by the Purchaser and SunGard in connection with the Offer, and which is incorporated in this Offer to Purchase by reference.

If SunGard uses funds under the Credit
Agreements in connection with the acquisition of HTE, SunGard intends to repay borrowings under the Credit Agreements from working capital and funds provided by future operations, and to refinance any outstanding borrowings on or prior to any
applicable maturity date. While SunGard has no specific arrangements in this regard at this time, SunGard currently expects that if necessary it will be able to obtain any refinancing on commercially reasonable terms at the time. 

The Purchaser believes that the financial condition of SunGard
and its affiliates is not material to a decision by a holder of shares of HTE common stock whether to tender such shares in the Offer because (i) cash is the only consideration that will be paid to the holders of HTE common stock in connection with
the Offer and the Merger, (ii) the Purchaser is offering to purchase all of the outstanding shares of HTE common stock in the Offer, (iii) the Offer is not subject to any financing arrangements or financing contingencies, and (iv) SunGard has
sufficient cash on hand and cash equivalents, or has sufficient availability under its existing line of credit, to provide the Purchaser with the amount of cash consideration payable to holders of HTE common stock in the Offer and the Merger.

11.    Background of the Offer 

Background 

The following information was prepared by SunGard and HTE. Information about HTE was provided by HTE, and neither the Purchaser nor SunGard has verified the accuracy or completeness of any information regarding meetings or
discussions in which SunGard or its representatives did not participate. 

On August 8, 2002, Jeffrey Feather, chairman of SunGard Pentamation, a SunGard subsidiary, contacted by telephone L.A. Gornto, Jr., executive vice president and general counsel of HTE, to inquire whether HTE would be
interested in having preliminary discussions with respect to a potential acquisition of HTE by SunGard. 

As a result of this contact, on August 27, 2002, Mr. Feather, together with Richard Tarbox, senior vice presidentcorporate
development of SunGard, and Robert Clarke, chief executive officer of SunGard Public Sector and Non-Profit Group, met with Bernard Markey, chairman of HTE, to discuss SunGards preliminary interest in a possible acquisition of HTE. During this
meeting, a possible transaction was discussed only in general terms, and no indicative price in such transaction was discussed. 

On September 3, 2002, Mr. Markey telephoned Mr. Clarke to indicate that HTEs board of directors had authorized HTEs management
to conduct preliminary acquisition discussions with SunGard. 

On September 5, 2002, SunGard executed a confidentiality agreement with HTE. 

On September 9, 2002, Mr. Markey and Joseph Loughry, president and chief executive officer of HTE, met at SunGards offices with Messrs. Tarbox, Clarke and Feather and Bruce Langston, chief
financial officer of SunGard Public Sector and Non-Profit Group. During this meeting, Mr. Loughry gave a general overview of HTEs business. Mr. Markey gave an update on the status of ongoing litigation concerning the HTE common stock held by
Tyler Technologies, Inc. (Tyler Litigation). Mr. Loughry and Mr. Markey indicated to SunGard that before HTE would proceed with discussions, SunGard would need to propose a valuation of HTE. The parties then discussed the possible next
steps that could enable SunGard to determine a preliminary valuation of HTE. 



On September
11, 2002, Mr. Markey, via e-mail, provided Mr. Tarbox with both HTEs forecast of its operating results for the quarter ending September 30, 2002 and a summary of the estimate of the annual expenses that could be saved if HTE were to cease
operating as a public company. 

On September 17,
2002, Mr. Tarbox, in a phone discussion with Mr. Markey, indicated that, based upon available public information of HTE and the financial information that HTE had provided, SunGard considered HTEs enterprise value (prior to consideration of
any excess cash or debt) to be $85.0 million. Following that discussion, Messrs. Markey and Tarbox had a subsequent phone conversation in which Mr. Markey indicated that, after conferring with HTEs board of directors, HTE considered HTEs
enterprise value to be higher than what SunGard had indicated. 

On September 18, 2002, as part of a regularly scheduled meeting, the HTE board of directors decided that due to the uncertainty concerning the Tyler Litigation, it was best to defer any further acquisition discussions with SunGard
and another interested third party at that time. 

On September 19, 2002, Mr. Markey telephoned Mr. Tarbox at SunGard and informed him of the decision of the HTE board of directors to defer acquisition discussions at that time until a court decision was rendered in the Tyler
Litigation. 

On September 23, 2002, HTE received
notice that the Federal Court having jurisdiction in the Tyler Litigation had entered an order on September 18, 2002 holding that HTEs redemption of the HTE common stock held by Tyler was invalid and no longer effective (the
Order), and on September 24, 2002 HTE issued a press release regarding the Order. 

On October 4, 2002, the board of directors of HTE held a telephonic meeting to discuss whether HTE should engage an investment banking firm to advise it on various strategic alternatives available,
including a possible sale or merger transaction. The Board agreed that an investment banking firm should be engaged by HTE at this time to assist and advise HTE as to its strategic alternatives, including a possible sale or merger of HTE.

Between October 4 and 11, 2002, HTE had
discussions with Broadview International LLC (Broadview) and formally confirmed that the financial advisory agreement between HTE and Broadview, dated September 2, 1999, remained in effect and in full force. HTE and Broadview then
entered into an amendment to the financial advisory agreement dated as of October 11, 2002 and the HTE board of directors then authorized Broadview to approach certain potential strategic and financial partners in order to assess the viability of a
business combination. 

In mid-October 2002, Mr.
Markey subsequently telephoned Mr. Tarbox to indicate that HTEs board of directors had engaged Broadview to advise HTE in exploring strategic alternatives, including a possible acquisition of all of HTEs common stock. SunGard
subsequently received a booklet of information concerning HTE, including financial projections for the quarter ending December 31, 2002 and for the fiscal year 2003 and a projection of HTEs balance sheet as of December 31, 2002. 

On October 21, 2002, Mr. Tarbox telephoned Scott Sedlacek of
Broadview and indicated that SunGard was interested in having discussions relating to a business combination with HTE. 

On October 22, 2002, the Board held a telephonic meeting to discuss 18 companies identified by Broadview as potential acquirors of HTE and
to develop a plan of action to deal with discussions with these companies. Based on the advice of Broadview as to each company identified, HTEs board of directors instructed Broadview to approach and explore the interest of 12 companies within
the next two weeks. 

From late October through
November 2002, Broadview contacted several companies with HTEs approval to ascertain their potential interest in pursuing a business combination with HTE. During this time, Broadview, via telephone, regularly updated members of the HTE board
of directors regarding the status of the ongoing process of evaluating potential suitors for a business combination. As a result of Broadviews discussions with prospective companies, representatives of HTE and Broadview held informational
meetings with, and provided certain financial information to, several potential acquirors, during the period from early November 2002 to early January 2003. 



On November
12, 2002, Mr. Tarbox received a communication via e-mail from Mr. Sedlacek that provided instructions on how SunGard should respond in writing if SunGard had interest in submitting a preliminary indication of interest for a cash purchase of all of
HTEs outstanding shares and outstanding vested and unvested stock options. 

On November 15, 2002, in response to a request from Broadview, Constellation Software, Inc. (Constellation) submitted to Broadview a preliminary indication of interest to acquire all of the
outstanding common stock of HTE for a cash purchase price of $4.50 per share. The indication of interest was subject to Constellations satisfactory completion of a due diligence review of HTE. Broadview agreed to present the proposal for
consideration to the HTE board of directors, and to provide feedback to representatives of Constellation. 

On November 18, 2002, based upon the information provided by HTE and publicly available information, SunGard submitted to Broadview a
non-binding letter of interest to acquire HTE for a cash purchase price in the range of $5.00 to $5.25 per share plus an amount not to exceed $12.0 million to acquire all of HTEs outstanding vested and unvested options. This expression of
interest was subject both to SunGards satisfactory completion of a due diligence review of HTE and to receiving the approval of SunGards board of directors. Broadview agreed to present the proposal for consideration to the HTE board of
directors, and to provide feedback to representatives of SunGard. 

On November 20, 2002, Mr. Sedlacek indicated to Mr. Tarbox in a phone discussion that SunGards valuation of the shares of HTE was lower than what HTEs board of directors considered to be the appropriate valuation
of HTE based upon commonly used indices of valuation for recent comparable transactions of public companies. Messrs. Sedlacek and Tarbox also discussed the appropriate amount of cash in excess of normal operating cash requirements that SunGard
should consider in determining its valuation of the shares of HTE. 

On November 22, 2002, HTE issued a press release announcing that it had received indications of interest in business combinations at a premium to the current trading price of the HTE common stock, and had re-engaged
Broadview to provide strategic financial advice to HTE, including evaluating the initial approaches as well as additional proposals from strategic and financial buyers. HTE also disclosed that it had received the preliminary indication of interest
from Constellation, as well as several other indications of interest from qualified buyers at cash prices higher than Constellations proposed bid of $4.50 per share. 

On November 25, 2002, Messrs. Sedlacek and Tarbox had a further conversation in which Mr. Sedlacek indicated
that, because the cost to acquire HTEs outstanding options would be less than SunGards estimate based upon its indicative valuation of the per-share price of HTEs common stock, that HTE considered SunGards then-current
valuation of HTEs shares to be a range of $5.25 to $5.50. Mr. Sedlacek further indicated that, based upon the significant amount of excess cash in HTE, the board of directors of HTE considered SunGards preliminary indication of value to
be too low to consider SunGards proposal any further. 

On November 26, 2002, Mr. Tarbox verbally proposed to Mr. Sedlacek a cash price in the range of $6.00 per share as a basis for continuing discussions with HTE. Mr. Sedlacek agreed to present the proposal for consideration to the HTE
board of directors and to provide feedback to Mr. Tarbox. 

On December 3, 2002, Mr. Tarbox verbally reiterated to Mr. Sedlacek a cash price in the range of $6.00 per share as a basis for continued discussions with HTE. 

On December 3 and 10, 2002, Messrs. Sedlacek and Tarbox had further conversations concerning both the
appropriate valuation of HTEs shares and that HTE had received indications of interest from other third parties at amounts higher than what SunGard had indicated. 

On December 11, 2002, Mr. Sedlacek in a telephone conversation indicated to Mr. Tarbox that, based upon other
indications of interest and the valuation that the board of directors of HTE considered to be the appropriate valuation of HTE, SunGard would need to consider proposing a minimum cash price of $6.50 per share for HTEs shares. 



On December
16, 2002, Mr. Tarbox indicated in a telephone conversation with Mr. Sedlacek that SunGard was prepared to increase its proposal to acquire HTEs share to $6.50 per share. Messrs. Sedlacek and Tarbox agreed to arrange to have representatives
from SunGard meet with representatives of HTE to conduct further due diligence, concentrating on HTEs results of operations for 2002 and financial projections for 2003. 

On December 18, 2002, Mr. Markey and Mr. Loughry invited Mr. Tarbox and other representatives of SunGard to
conduct confirmatory due diligence. Mr. Loughry indicated that other interested third parties had conducted more detailed on-site due diligence than SunGard had conducted to that point and that the board of directors of HTE was concerned about the
certainty of SunGards new proposal given the amount of SunGards due diligence to date relative to other interested parties. 

On December 20, 2002, SunGard submitted a request for information to be received in advance of this due diligence meeting. On December 30,
2002, HTE provided this information to SunGard. 

On January 3, 2003, Messrs. Clarke, Feather and Langston and Donald Appleton, president of SunGard Pentamation, met with Mr. Loughery and Susan Falatico, chief financial officer of HTE, to review HTEs preliminary financial
results for the fiscal year 2002 and its 2003 projections. 

On January 9, 2003, Mr. Sedlacek in a telephone conversation with Mr. Tarbox indicated that another party had proposed a purchase of HTEs shares for a cash price in excess of SunGards proposal of $6.50 per share.

On January 10, 2003, based upon the information
provided by HTE and publicly available information, representatives of SunGard verbally proposed to Broadview a cash price in the range of $7.00 per share as a basis for continuing discussions with HTE. At Broadviews suggestion, SunGard
submitted a written proposal to Broadview indicating their interest to acquire all of the outstanding HTE shares for a cash price of $7.00 per share. Later that day, Broadview indicated to representatives of SunGard that the board of directors of
HTE was interested in pursuing negotiation of the proposed transaction, including a definitive agreement, at a cash price of $7.00 per share. 

Between January 13, 2003 and January 31, 2003, representatives of SunGard and its legal and accounting advisors conducted extensive due
diligence on HTEs business, including conducting meetings with HTEs management and reviewing financial and legal documents provided by HTE. Also during this time, legal and financial representatives of SunGard and HTE and their
respective advisors discussed and negotiated on many occasions all aspects of the proposed merger and the merger agreement therefor. These negotiations covered all aspects of the transaction, including, among other things: the representations and
warranties made by the parties; the restrictions on the conduct of HTEs business following execution and delivery of the Merger Agreement; the conditions to completion of the Offer and the Merger; the provisions regarding termination; the
details of the fiduciary out provisions; the amount, triggers and payment of the termination fee and the consequences of termination; and the delivery and terms of the Tender and Voting Agreements. 

On January 31, 2003, the board of directors of SunGard
approved the Merger Agreement in the form presented. 

On February 1, 2003, the board of directors of HTE met telephonically to review and consider the final terms of the transaction. Participating in the meeting were all members of the Board, HTE management and representatives of
Broadview and Greenberg Traurig, P.A., HTEs legal counsel. A representative of Greenberg Traurig reviewed with the HTE board of directors the principal provisions of the proposed Merger Agreement and Tender and Voting Agreements.
Representatives of Broadview presented Broadviews fairness opinion to the HTE board of directors that as of the date of the meeting and based upon and subject to certain matters stated in such opinion, the $7.00 per share cash offer price was
fair, from a financial point of view, to holders of HTE common stock. The Broadview representatives described the procedures followed, Broadviews findings, the bases and methods of arriving at Broadviews fairness opinion, including the
financial analysis Broadview made 



of certain information supporting its fairness opinion, and responded to questions from the directors. The HTE board of directors then
affirmed that the Merger was fair to, and in the best interests of, HTEs shareholders, declared the Merger advisable, approved the proposed terms of the Offer, Merger, the Merger Agreement and the Tender and Voting Agreements in substantially
the forms presented, and resolved to recommend that HTEs shareholders accept the Offer and tender their shares in the Offer. 

On February 4, 2003, the Merger Agreement was executed by SunGard, the Purchaser and HTE and the Tender and Voting Agreements were
executed by the shareholders named therein, SunGard and the Purchaser. 

On February 5, 2003, before the opening of trading on the New York Stock Exchange and Nasdaq, SunGard and HTE issued a joint press release announcing the transaction. 

Reasons for SunGard Entering into the Merger Agreement

At a meeting held on January 31, 2003,
SunGards board of directors approved the transaction, subject to satisfactory negotiation of the Merger Agreement. In approving the transaction, SunGards board of directors consulted with SunGards management and legal advisors. The
board considered, among other things, the following: 



the strategic fit between SunGards Public Sector and Non-Profit Systems Group and HTE, including: the benefits that SunGards financial resources could
provide to HTE; the opportunity to cross-sell SunGard and HTE products into the others customer base; and the opportunity to provide a broad range of products and services to public sector-industry customers; 



the opportunity to realize certain cost synergies from combining HTE with SunGards Public Sector and Non-Profit Systems Group, including the savings resulting
from HTE no longer being an independent public company; 



prospects for the demand for software systems solutions and services in the public sector industry; 



the quality and state of development of HTEs products and the reputation of HTE in the public sector industry; and 



the provisions of the Merger Agreement, including the price, respective representations, warranties and covenants of the parties. 

12.    Purpose of the Offer; Plans for HTE; The Merger Agreement; The Tender and Voting Agreements 

Purpose of the Offer 

The purpose of the Offer and Merger is to enable SunGard to acquire the entire equity interest in, and thus control of, HTE. The Offer, as
the first step in the acquisition of HTE, is intended to facilitate the acquisition of all the outstanding shares of HTE common stock or, if less, all shares of HTE common stock that are tendered in the Offer and not properly withdrawn prior to the
Expiration Date, subject to the conditions to the Offer described in Section 13 (Certain Conditions to the Offer) of this Offer to Purchase. The purpose of the Merger is to acquire any and all outstanding shares of HTE common stock that are not
tendered in the Offer and accepted for payment by the Purchaser in the Offer. 

Plans for HTE 

If the Minimum Condition and the other conditions to the Offer described in Section 13 (Certain Conditions to the Offer) of this Offer to Purchase have been satisfied and the Purchaser purchases the shares of HTE common stock that
are tendered in the Offer, SunGard intends and will have the right to designate representatives to HTEs board of directors who will constitute at least a majority of the board of directors and therefore control HTE. Following successful
completion of the Offer and the Merger, SunGard intends to integrate HTEs operations with those of SunGard under the direction of SunGard management. SunGards principal reason for 



acquiring HTE is to expand its integrated software solutions for the public sector industry. SunGard intends to continue to review HTE and
its assets, corporate structure, dividend policy, capitalization, operations, properties, policies, management and personnel and, subject to the terms of the Merger Agreement, to consider whether any changes would be desirable in light of the
circumstances then existing, and reserves the right to take such actions or effect such changes as it deems desirable. Except as disclosed in this Offer to Purchase, neither the Purchaser nor SunGard has any present plans or proposals that would
result in an extraordinary corporate transaction, such as a merger, reorganization, liquidation, relocation of operations or sale or transfer of assets, involving HTE or any of its subsidiaries, or any material changes in HTEs corporate
structure or business. The Purchaser will honor all obligations under all existing employment agreements and has not entered into any employment or employment-related agreements in connection with the Offer. 

The Merger Agreement 

The following is a summary of the Merger Agreement. The
following summary does not purport to be a complete description of the terms and conditions of the Merger Agreement and is qualified in its entirety by reference to the Merger Agreement, a copy of which is filed as an exhibit to the Tender Offer
Statement on Schedule TO that has been filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission by the Purchaser and SunGard in connection with the Offer. A copy of the Merger Agreement has been provided to each shareholder as Appendix A to this Offer to
Purchase pursuant to Section 607.1104 of the Florida Business Corporation Act (the FBCA) relating to short-form mergers. If the Purchaser acquires more than 80% of the outstanding common stock of HTE, it intends to effect a short-form
merger pursuant to Section 607.1104 of the FBCA without a meeting or vote of the HTE shareholders. See Section 14 (Certain Legal Matters) for more information. You should read the Merger Agreement in its entirety for a more complete description of
the matters summarized below. 

The Offer

The Merger Agreement provides for the
commencement of the Offer. The Purchasers obligation to accept for payment shares of HTE common stock that are tendered in the Offer is subject to the satisfaction or waiver, if permitted under the Merger Agreement, of each of the conditions
to the Offer that are described in Section 13 (Certain Conditions to the Offer) of this Offer to Purchase. The Purchaser may not, without HTEs prior written consent, make any change to the terms and conditions of the Offer that (i) decreases
the Offer Price, (ii) changes the form of consideration to be paid in the Offer, (iii) changes the number of shares of HTE common stock sought in the Offer, (iv) imposes new conditions to the Offer in addition to those described in Section 13 of
this Offer to Purchase, (v) extends the Offer except as provided for in the Merger Agreement and described below, (vi) amends or waives the Minimum Condition or (vii) is adverse to the holders of shares of HTE common stock. 

If at any then-scheduled expiration date of the Offer, any of
the conditions to the Offer have not been satisfied or waived, the Purchaser is entitled to extend the Offer for such amount of time as is reasonably necessary to cause such conditions to the Offer to be satisfied. Additionally, the Purchaser may
(but is not required to) extend the Offer (one or more times) for an aggregate additional period of not more than 20 business days if the number of shares of HTE common stock that have been validly tendered (and not withdrawn) as of the scheduled or
extended expiration date of the Offer (plus any such shares of HTE common stock tendered under the Tender and Voting Agreements and any shares of HTE common stock with respect to which SunGard or Purchaser has sole beneficial ownership)
represent more than a majority of HTEs Adjusted Outstanding Shares, but less than 80% of HTEs Adjusted Outstanding Shares as of such date or, if greater, the number and type of shares of common stock including shares of common stock
entitled to vote and shares of common stock not entitled to vote, required to satisfy the conditions of the FBCA relating to short-form mergers. See Section 14 (Certain Legal Matters) for more information. 

If any of the conditions to the Offer have not been satisfied
or waived at any then-scheduled expiration date of the Offer, the Purchaser has agreed to extend the Offer by 10 business days, if so requested by HTE in writing; provided, however, that the Purchaser is not required to extend the expiration date
more than one time pursuant to this provision. 



The Purchaser
also may (but is not required to) provide for a subsequent offering period (within the meaning of Rule 14d-11 under the Exchange Act) of at least three but not more than 20 business days following the expiration of the Offer. 

The Merger Agreement further provides that the Purchaser will,
on the terms and subject to the conditions to the Offer, accept for payment, and pay for, all the shares of HTE common stock that are validly tendered and not properly withdrawn in the Offer as promptly as practicable after the Expiration Date. If
the Purchaser provides for a subsequent offering period, subject to the terms and conditions of the Merger Agreement, the Purchaser will accept for payment, and pay for, all shares of HTE common stock that are validly tendered during the subsequent
offering period as promptly as practicable after such shares are tendered. 

Appointment of Directors after Acceptance of Shares Tendered in the Offer 

The Merger Agreement provides that, effective upon acceptance for payment of any shares of HTE common stock in the Offer, SunGard shall be
entitled to designate the number of directors, rounded up to the next whole number, on HTEs board of directors that equals the product of (i) the total number of directors on HTEs board of directors (giving effect to the election of any
additional directors pursuant to these provisions) and (ii) a fraction whose numerator is the aggregate number of shares of HTE common stock then beneficially owned by SunGard or Purchaser (including shares of HTE common stock accepted for payment
pursuant to the Offer), and whose denominator is the total number of shares of HTE common stock then outstanding. 

The Merger Agreement further provides that following a request by SunGard, HTE must take all commercially reasonable actions necessary to
cause the individuals designated by SunGard to be elected or appointed to HTEs board of directors, including, if necessary, either increasing the size of HTEs board of directors or securing the resignations of then incumbent directors.
Furthermore, pursuant to the terms of the Merger Agreement, HTE must take all commercially reasonable actions necessary to cause the individuals so designated by SunGard to constitute substantially the same percentage (rounding up where appropriate)
as is on HTEs board of directors on (i) each committee of HTEs board of directors, (ii) each board of directors of each subsidiary of HTE and (iii) each committee of each such board of directors of each subsidiary of HTE. The Merger
Agreement requires that at all times until the completion of the Merger, SunGard and HTE shall use their respective commercially reasonable efforts to cause at least two of the members of HTEs board of directors to be individuals who were
directors of HTE and were not officers or employees of HTE or any of its subsidiaries on the date of the Merger Agreement (the Continuing Directors). 

Notwithstanding anything in the Merger Agreement to the contrary, after the election or appointment of the
directors designated by SunGard to HTEs board of directors and prior to the completion of the Merger, under the terms of the Merger Agreement, the approval of the Continuing Directors will be required to (i) amend or terminate the Merger
Agreement on behalf of HTE, (ii) extend the time for performance by SunGard or the Purchaser of, or waive compliance by HTE with, any of the agreements or conditions contained in the Merger Agreement for the benefit of HTE, (iii) authorize any
required or permitted consent or action by HTEs board of directors under the Merger Agreement or (iv) authorize any other action of HTE under the Merger Agreement which adversely affects the holders of shares of HTE common stock (other than
SunGard or the Purchaser); provided, that if for any reason there are no Continuing Directors and HTE has used commercially reasonable efforts to appoint Continuing Directors, such actions may be effected by majority vote of HTEs entire board
of directors. 

The Merger 

The Merger Agreement provides that, following the satisfaction
or waiver of the conditions to the Merger described below under the caption Conditions to the Merger, the Purchaser will be merged with and into HTE in accordance with the applicable provision of Florida law, HTE will continue as the
surviving corporation of the Merger and the separate corporate existence of the Purchaser will cease. 



Articles of
Incorporation and Bylaws of the Surviving Corporation 

The Merger Agreement provides that upon the completion of the Merger, the articles of incorporation of HTE, other than those provisions with respect to indemnification of directors and officers, shall be amended and restated to
conform to the articles of incorporation of the Purchaser, as in effect immediately prior to the completion of the Merger. The bylaws of HTE, other than those with respect to indemnification of directors and officers of HTE, will be amended and
restated to conform to the bylaws of the Purchaser as in effect immediately prior to the completion of the Merger. 

Directors and Officers of the Surviving Corporation 

Under the terms of the Merger Agreement, upon the completion of the Merger, the directors of HTE will be the
directors of the Purchaser immediately prior to the completion of the Merger, and the officers of HTE will be the officers of HTE immediately prior to the completion of the Merger. 

Conversion of Shares of HTE Common Stock 

Pursuant to the Merger Agreement, each share of HTE common stock that is issued and outstanding immediately
prior to the completion of the Merger (other than shares owned by SunGard, the Purchaser or HTE or any wholly owned subsidiary of SunGard or HTE which shares will be canceled without any consideration), will be converted into the right to receive
$7.00, the price per share paid in the Offer in cash, without interest thereon. 

Dissenters Rights 

Under Section 607.1302(4) of the FBCA, because HTEs common stock is listed on the Nasdaq National Market, no shareholder of HTE will be entitled to exercise dissenters rights under the FBCA
in connection with the transactions contemplated by the Merger Agreement, including the Offer and the Merger. 

Treatment of HTE Options 

Each holder of an option to purchase common stock of HTE (each a Company Option) will be entitled to receive in settlement of
each Company Option an amount equal to the product of (i) the excess, if any, of the Offer Price over the exercise price per share of such Company Option and (ii) the number of shares subject to such Company Option, less applicable tax withholdings.
Except as otherwise agreed to by SunGard and HTE, all stock option plans established by HTE or any of its subsidiaries shall terminate as of the date of the Merger and the provisions in any other plan, program or arrangement providing for the
issuance or grant of any other interest in respect of the capital stock of HTE or any subsidiary of HTE shall be deleted, terminated and of no further force or effect as of the date of the Merger.

Purchaser and SunGard in the Merger Agreement, including representations relating to: 



organization; 



capital stock and ownership; 



financial and corporate records; 



compliance with law;

sections 607.0901 and 607.0902 of the FBCA not applicable;
